---
layout: "post"
title: "HoTT exercises"
date: "2018-04-08"
categories: type-theory
toc: true
---

This is a self-contained version of some solutions for HoTT-Book's exercises.
The idea is to unpackage all as long as possible to get a better understanding.
Many changes can appear running this experiment. Solutions are
type-checked as a whole using Agda v2.5.3.

## Requirements

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agda has a pragma to work with HoTT:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="516" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="520" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="528" class="Option">--without-K</a> <a id="540" class="Symbol">#-}</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Equality type definition also called Identity type:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="703" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="709" class="Number">4</a> <a id="711" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">_≡_</a>

## Chapter 1

### Exercise 1.1

<div class="exercise">
Given functions $$f : A \to B$$ and $$g:B\to C$$, define
their composite $$ g\circ f:A\to C$$.
Show that we have $$h \circ (g\circ f) \equiv (h\circ g)\circ f$$.
</div>

We define the composition operation in Agda as follows.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="_∘_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">_∘_</a> <a id="2113" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2115" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="2117" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2118" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2118" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="2120" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2120" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="2122" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2122" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2123" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="2125" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2126" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2126" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2128" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2130" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2134" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2118" class="Bound">i</a><a id="2135" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2137" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2137" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2139" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2141" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2145" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2120" class="Bound">j</a><a id="2146" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2148" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2148" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="2150" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2152" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2156" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2122" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2157" class="Symbol">}</a>
    <a id="2163" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2165" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2166" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2137" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2168" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2170" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2148" class="Bound">C</a><a id="2171" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2177" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2179" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2180" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2126" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2182" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2184" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2137" class="Bound">B</a><a id="2185" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2191" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2193" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2126" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2195" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2197" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2148" class="Bound">C</a>
<a id="2199" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2199" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2201" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">∘</a> <a id="2203" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2203" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2205" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="2207" class="Symbol">λ</a> <a id="2209" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2209" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="2211" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2213" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2199" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2215" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2216" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2203" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2218" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2209" class="Bound">x</a><a id="2219" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Then, the `∘-assoc` shows us that associativity of this composition holds.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="∘-assoc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%88%98-assoc" class="Function">∘-assoc</a> <a id="2330" class="Symbol">:</a> <a ### Exercise 1.2

<div class="exercise">
Derive the recursion principle for products $$\mathsf{rec}_{A\times B}$$
using only the projections, and verify that the definitional equalities
are valid. Do the same for $$\Sigma$$-types.
</div>

To solve this problem we need to know:

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}
      : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) → A \times B \to C.
    $$
    </p>

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}
      : \prod\limits_{(C : U)} (\Pi_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C) \rightarrow
        \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C
    $$
    </p>

<div class="proof" id="proof-1.2">
Proof.<br/>
For products:<br/>
If we have the projections,
$$\mathsf{proj}_1 : A \times B \to \mathsf{A}$$ and $$\mathsf{proj}_2 : A \times B \to \mathsf{B}$$,
then $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$ is another inhabitant where

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
&\mathsf{rec}_1 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) \to A \times B \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_1~C~g~c~:\equiv~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c,~\mathsf{proj}_2 c).
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_1$$.
<br/>
<br/>
For sums:<br/>
The projections are $$\mathsf{proj}_1 : \sum_{x : A}  Bx \to \mathsf{A}$$ and
$$\mathsf{proj}_2 :  \prod_{(p : \sum_{x : A}  Bx)} \to \mathsf{B} (\mathsf{proj}_1 p)$$.<br/>
By using these projections, we got another recursor defined as follows:
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{aling*}
&\mathsf{rec}_2 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}}  (\prod_{x : A} Bx \to C) \to \sum\limits_{x : A} B x \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_2~C~g~c~=~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c)~(\mathsf{proj}_2 c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>

By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$.
</div>

the following exercises including this one:

Its recursor with a function $$g : \prod_{(x : A)} B(x)\rightarrow C$$
that we provide.

  <a id="5333" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="5338" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Def₁</a> <a id="5345" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="5351" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5352" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5354" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5356" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a><a id="5361" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5363" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%82" class="Field">proj₂</a><a id="5368" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5370" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="5374" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="Σ-Rec₁.rec" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="5383" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5385" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5387" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5250" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5389" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5261" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="5391" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="5393" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5276" class="Bound">C</a>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the other hand, the product type is just a particular case of the sigma type
when the codomain is not dependent, as we can see next by omitting the argument
in `(λ _ → B)`.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="5779" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">×-Def₁</a> <a id="5793" class="Keyword">where</a>

Its recursor with a function $$g : A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C$$ that we provide.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6015" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Rec₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Rec%E2%82%81" ### Exercise 1.3

<p class="exercise">
Derive the induction principle for products $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$,
using only the projections and the propositional uniqueness principle
$$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$.
Verify that the definitional equalities are valid.
</p>

To solve this problem, recall the uniqueness principle (Pp. 29. HoTT-Book)

- The **propositional uniqueness principle** says that
every element of $$A\times B$$ is equal to a pair.

<p class="equation">
  $$ \mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}
     : \prod_{(x : A \times B)} ((\mathsf{proj}_{1}(x) , \mathsf{proj}_{2}(x))
       \equiv_{A\times B} x).
  $$
</p>

Product type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6946" class="Comment">-- this would be trivial in agda due to definitional η for records</a>
<a id="7013" class="Comment">-- so Capriotti defined a product type without η:</a>
<a id="7063" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="7077" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="7835" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a> <a id="7844" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7849" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7851" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>

        <a id="7909" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7911" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7882" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7913" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7915" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7884" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7917" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7919" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7892" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="7921" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7923" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7894" class="Bound">z</a> <a id="7925" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7927" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7928" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7882" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7930" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7932" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7892" class="Bound">y</a><a id="7933" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7935" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7937" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7938" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7884" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7940" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7942" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7894" class="Bound">z</a><a id="7943" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="7947" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.pair%3D" class="Function">pair=</a> <a id="7953" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7958" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7963" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7965" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The induction principle for the product type:

<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B} : \prod\limits_{C : A \times B \to \mathcal{U}}
  \left( \prod\limits_{x:A}\ \prod\limits_{y:B}\ \,C( (x,y) ) \right)
  \to \prod\limits_{x:A \times B}\ \,C(x)
$$
</p>

          <a id="8580" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8582" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8583" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8583" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8585" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8587" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8588" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8588" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8590" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8592" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8279" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8593" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8595" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8595" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8597" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8599" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8290" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8600" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8602" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8604" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8551" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8606" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8607" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8588" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8609" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8611" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8595" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8612" class="Symbol">))</a>

          <a id="8652" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8654" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind" class="Function">ind</a> <a id="8658" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8551" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8660" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8583" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8662" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8663" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8628" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8665" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8667" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8635" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8668" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8670" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="8672" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8583" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8674" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8628" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8676" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8635" class="Bound">y</a>
  <a id="8680" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind-%CE%B2" class="Function">ind-β</a> <a id="8686" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8686" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8688" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8688" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8690" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8690" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8692" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8692" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8694" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8696" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

<p class="exercise">
Generalize $$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$ to Σ-types, and do the same for
$$\Sigma$$-types, i.e. show induction and verify the definitional equality
is valid.
</p>

Σ-type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="8944" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Def₂</a> <a id="8958" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="Σ-Def₂.Σ._,_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="9034" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9036" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9037" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9037" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9039" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9041" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8980" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9042" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9044" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9046" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8991" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9048" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9037" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9050" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9052" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3" class="Datatype">Σ</a> <a id="9054" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8980" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9056" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8991" class="Bound">B</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Its induction principle:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="9439" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Ind₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Ind%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Ind₂</a> <a id="9453" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9454" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9454" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="9456" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9456" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9457" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9459" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9459" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9461" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9463" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9467" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9454" class="Bound">i</a><a id="9468" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9470" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9470" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9472" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9474" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9459" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9476" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9478" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9482" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9456" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9483" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9485" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="9493" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="9498" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Def₂</a> <a id="9505" class="Keyword">public</a>

### Exercise 1.4

<div class="exercise">
Assuming as given only the <em>iterator</em> for natural numbers
<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ite} : \prod\limits_{C:\mathcal{U}} C \to (C \to C) \to \mathbb{N} \to C $$
</p>
with the defining equations
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,0)               &\equiv c_0, \\
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,\mathsf{suc}(n)) &\equiv c_s(\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
derive a function having the type of the recursor $$\mathsf{rec}$$.
Show that the defining equations of the recursor hold propositionally for this
function, using the induction principle for $$\mathbb{N}$$.
</div>

To solve this problem, let us define the recursor and also the induction principle
for natural numbers. (See more details about these functions in
[Induction on Natural Numbers]({% post_url 2018-02-12-induction-on-natural-numbers %})).

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="10757" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="ℕ-Def" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a> <a id="10770" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="ℕ-Def.ℕ.suc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a>  <a id="10820" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10822" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a> <a id="10824" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="10826" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a>

  <a id="11001" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="11006" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a>

       <a id="11043" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11045" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11046" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11023" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11048" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a><a id="11052" class="Symbol">)</a>
       <a id="11061" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11063" class="Symbol">(∀</a> <a id="11066" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11067" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11067" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11069" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11071" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="11072" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="11074" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11076" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11023" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11078" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11067" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11080" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11082" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11023" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11084" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11085" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a> <a id="11089" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11067" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11090" class="Symbol">))</a>

Now, we define the iterator following the equations above:

Then, we now can define the recursor using this `ite` by iterating over the type
`ℕ × C` (*reloading recursion*?).


<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="11610" class="Comment">-- recursor</a>
  <a id="11624" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="11629" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="11636" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="11642" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11643" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">_×_</a><a id="11646" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11648" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%81" class="Function">proj₁</a><a id="11653" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11655" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">proj₂</a><a id="11660" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11662" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a><a id="11665" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="11723" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Fun.rec%E2%82%82" class="Function">rec₂</a> <a id="11728" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11728" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11730" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11730" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="11733" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11733" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="11736" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11736" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11738" class="Symbol">=</a>

           <a id="11770" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11771" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a> <a id="11776" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="11778" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11730" class="Bound">c₀</a><a id="11780" class="Symbol">)</a>
           <a id="11793" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="11796" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11797" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11797" class="Bound">p</a> <a            <a id="11863" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11736" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11864" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, we need to establish the propositional equality between these two
definitions of recursor, i.e, between `rec` and `rec₂`. Let's use
induction to prove that.

      <a id="12754" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12690" class="Function">u</a> <a id="12756" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12758" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a>  <a id="12768" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12769" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="12771" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12773" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="12774" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="12776" class="Argument">B</a> <a id="12778" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12780" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12393" class="Bound">C</a><a id="12781" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12783" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12784" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#ex1-4.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="12790" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12393" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="12792" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12395" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="12795" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12398" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="12798" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12406" class="Bound">n</a><a id="12799" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


### Exercise 1.5

<div class="exercise">

Show that if we define

  $$A+B :\equiv \sum\limits_{(x : \mathbbbold{2})} \mathsf{rec}_{\mathbbbold{2}} (\mathcal{U}, A , B, x),$$

then we can give a definition of $$\ind\limits_{A + B}$$ for which the
definitional equalities holds.

</div>

To solve this problem, let us introduce the $$\mathcal{2}$$ type, that is, the
type with two constructors also called **Bool**. The constructors are also called
false and true respectively.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="13304" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="13318" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="13327" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="13334" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13336" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="13340" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="13352" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13354" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟙" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="13362" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13364" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, let's try to define the recursor for this coproduct, and later,
we'll try the dependent version of it to complete the exercise.

      <a id="14563" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14565" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14500" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="14567" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="14569" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14502" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="14571" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14573" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14514" class="Bound">C</a>

  <a id="14601" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="14605" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14605" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14607" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14607" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14609" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14610" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="14612" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="14614" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14614" class="Bound">b</a><a id="14615" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14617" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14619" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14607" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14621" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14614" class="Bound">b</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Notice how the recursor of the coproduct matches with the elimination
rule of the disjunction conective also called *case analysis*. That's follows from the
[**propositions-as-types**](https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/propositions+as+types).

![path](/assets/latexit-images/disj-elimination.png)

Finally, the induction principle for the coproduct:

### Exercise 1.6

<div class="exercise" id="ex-1.6">
Show that if we define $$A \times B :≡ \prod_{x:\mathbf{2}}\mathsf{rec}_{\mathbf{2}}\ (\mathcal{U}\, A\, B\, x)$$,
then we can give a definition of $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$ for which the definitional
equalities propositionally (i.e. using equality types).
</div>

### Exercise 1.8

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.8">

Define multiplication and exponentiation using $$\mathsf{rec}{\mathbb{N}}$$.
Verify that $$(\mathbb{N},+,0,\times,1)$$ is a semiring using only
$$\ind{\mathbb{N}}$$.

</div>

### Exercise 1.9

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.9">

Define the type family $$\mathsf{Fin} : \mathbb{N} \to \mathcal{U}$$ mentioned
at the end of Section 1.3, and the dependent function $$\mathsf{fmax} :
\prod_{n:\mathbb{N}} \mathsf{Fin}(n+1)$$ mentioned in Section 1.4.
</div>

### Exercise 1.11

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.11">
Show that for any type $$A$$, we have $$\neg\neg\neg A \to \neg A$$.
</div>

### Exercise 1.16

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.16">
Show that addition of natural numbers is commutative:
<p class="equation">
$$
\prod\limits_{i,j : \mathbb{N}}\ (i + j = j + i).
$$
</p>
</div>

## Chapter 2

### Exercise 2.6

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.6">
Prove that if $$p : x \equiv y$$, then the function
$$(p \cdot -) : (y \equiv z) \to (x \equiv z)$$ is an equivalence.
</div>

### Exercise 2.10

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.10">
Prove that ∑-types are associative, in that for any $$A : \mathcal{U}$$
and families $$B : A  \to U$$ and $$C : \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \to \mathcal{U}$$,
we have
<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \simeq \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
</div>

<div class="proof" id="proof-2.10">
Solution.<br/>
We can prove that the following functions $$f$$ and $$g$$ are inverses.

<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \overset{f}{\underset{g}{\rightleftarrows}} \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
defined by $$f(a,b,c) :\equiv ((a,b),c)$$, $$g(z,c) :\equiv (\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)$$.<br/>
Indeed,
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(f \circ g) (z, c) &:\equiv f (g (z,c))\\
&:\equiv f\,(\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)\\
&:\equiv ((\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z), c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
</div>

### Exercise 2.13

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.13">
Show that $$(2 \simeq 2) \simeq 2$$.
</div>



### Exercise 2.14

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.14">
Suppose we add to type theory the equality reflection rule which says
that if there is an element $$p : x \equiv y$$, then in fact $$ x \equiv y$$.
Prove that for any $$p : x \equiv x$$ we have $$p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
</div>

### Exercise 2.17

<div class="exercise">
<ul>
  <li> Show that if $$A \simeq A$$  and $$B \simeq B'$$, then $$(A\times B) \simeq (A'\times B')$$. </li>
  <li> Give two proofs of this fact, one using univalence and one not using it, and show that the two proofs are equal.</li>
  <li> Formulate and prove analogous results for the other type formers: $$\Sigma$$, $$\to$$, $$\Pi$$, and $$+$$. </li>
</ul>
</div>



## Chapter 3

To solve the following exercises, let us recall a few things:

- The *set* definition in HoTT:

A type $$A$$ is a **set** if for all $$x, y : A$$ and
all $$p, q : x \equiv y$$, we have $$ p \equiv q$$. In a proposition
we have

$$
\mathsf{isSet}(A) :\equiv \prod\limits_{(x,y : A)}\prod\limits_{(p,q : x \equiv y)} (p \equiv q).
$$

- The type for equivalence from $$A$$ to $$B$$

$$
  (A \simeq B) :\equiv \sum\limits_{f : A \to B} \mathsf{isequiv}(f),
$$

where

$$
\mathsf{isequiv(f)} :\equiv
  \left (\sum\limits_{g : B \to A} (f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{B})\right) \times
  \left (\sum\limits_{h : B \to A} (h \circ f \sim \mathsf{id}_{A})\right)
$$

- The homotopy concept:

Let $$f , g : \prod\limits_{(x:A)} P(x)$$ be two sections of a
type family $$P : A \to \mathcal{U}$$. A **homotopy** from $$f$$ to $$g$$
is a dependent function of type

$$
(f \sim g) :\equiv \prod\limits_{x : A} (f(x) \equiv g(x)).
$$

### Exercise 3.1

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A\simeq B$$ and $$A$$ is a set, then so is $$B$$.
</div>


<div class="proof" id="proof-3.1">
Proof 1.<br/>
Let be $$x,y : B$$ and $$p : x \equiv_{B} y$$ and $$q : x \equiv_{B} y$$.
We need to prove $$ p \equiv q$$.<br/>
Since $$A\simeq B$$ then there is a function $$f : A \to B$$ and some
$$g : B \to A$$ such that $$f \circ g \sim id_{B}$$.
Using this function $$g$$ over the path $$p$$ we get
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} p : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
We do the same but this time over the path $$q$$, that is,
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} q : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
Because of $$A$$ is a set, we have a new path called
$$m :\mathsf{ap}_{g} p \equiv_{gx \equiv_{A} gy} \mathsf{ap}_{g} q$$. <br/>

Now, an action over this path $$m$$
using the function $$\mathsf{ap}_{f} : x \equiv_{A} y \to f x \equiv_{B} f y$$
will give us

<p class="equation">
$$
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m :
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q).
$$
</p>
By the lemmas in Chapter 2, we do the following reasoning:

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q) &=
  \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} q\\
  &=(\text{transporting by using} f \sim g)\\
  &=\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} q\\
  &=p \equiv q.
\end{align*}
$$<br/>
</p>
Then, we have the inhabitant, $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m : p \equiv q$$.
</div>

### Exercise 3.2

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A$$ and $$B$$ are sets, then so is $$A+B$$.
</div>

To solve this exercise, we should take a look of some results from Chapter 2,
Section 2.12.

<div class="proof" id="proof-3.2">
Proof.<br/>

Let be $$x, y : A + B$$, and paths $$p : x \equiv y$$, $$q : x \equiv
y$$. Let's get a path $$p \equiv q$$.  We proceed by case analysis. If
$$x :\equiv \mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, for
some $$a, b : A$$ then $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p : a
\equiv_{A} b$$ and $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q : a \equiv_{A}
b$$.

Since $$A$$ is a set, there is a path between these last two terms,
this is, $$m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p \equiv
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q$$.  Now, an action over this path
$$m$$ using the $$\mathsf{inl}$$ function give us:
$$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}} m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q)$$.<br/>

By path algebra we get $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
m : p \equiv q$$ since $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv p$$.<br/> Following the
same reasoning, we prove the case $$x :\equiv \mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y
:\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$.  For the latest cases, $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$ and $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, we use the
encode-decode method to derive a proof term for 𝟘 from
$$p$$ and $$q$$. Then, we may conclude anything we wish, that is, $$p
\equiv q$$.
</div>

In Agda.

  <a id="26206" class="Comment">-- ind : {A B : Set}</a>
  <a id="26229" class="Comment">--     → (C : A + B → Set)</a>
  <a id="26258" class="Comment">--     → ((x : A) → C (inl x))</a>
  <a id="26291" class="Comment">--     → ((x : B) → C (inr x))</a>
  <a id="26324" class="Comment">--     → (x : A + B) → C x</a>
  <a id="26353" class="Comment">-- ind C f g c x = {!   !}</a>

### Exercise 3.3

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$ A $$ is a set and $$B : A \to \mathcal{U}$$
is a type family such that $$B(x)$$ is a set for all
$$x : A$$, then $$\Sigma\limits_{(x:A)}\ B(x)$$ is a set.
</div>

### Exercise 3.4

<div class="exercise">
Show that $$A$$ is a mere proposition if and only
if $$A\to A$$ is contractible.
</div>
